Commentary

An Overview of the South Manchuria Railway (By Bin) (1) (Continued) 62

(III) Railways Operated Under the Control of the South Manchuria Railway 63

In the previous section, we have already mentioned that the Japanese, in order to complete their railway network plan in a disguised form, often used the name of Sino-Japanese cooperation to force investments in our country and build new roads, or forced contracts to be built. By the time the railway was completed, the debt was also high and could not be repaid. The Japanese further controlled their important positions, seeking only benefits for themselves and arbitrarily dominating them. Year after year, they were nominally owned by us, but in reality, they all fell into the hands of the Japanese.

The railways operated under the control of the South Manchuria Railway include the following lines:

(1) Jichang Line: From the provincial capital of Jilin to Changchun, a total length of 79.4 miles. Construction began three years before the founding of the Republic and was completed in the first year of the Republic. It was financed by loans from the South Manchuria Railway and managed by the South Manchuria Railway entrusted by our country. In reality, this road has been separated from our country and embedded in the scope of the South Manchuria Railway. It is the first railway sacrificed for our country's loan construction.

(2) Jitun Road: From Jilin to Dunhua, a total length of 131.0 miles. Construction started in June of the Republic Year 15 and was completed in October of the Republic Year 17. It was financed by loans from the South Manchuria Railway and contracted. The project was poorly constructed and expensive. The budgeted and settled amounts were arbitrarily changed. The actual road rights are entirely in the hands of the Japanese.

(3) Sipingjie-Taonan Railway (Sitao Road): The main line starts from Sipingjie and ends in Taonan. The branch line starts from Zhengjiatun and ends in Tongliao, totaling 264.6 miles long. Construction started in April of the Republic Year 5 and was completed in November of the Republic Year 12. It was financed by loans from the Yokohama Specie Bank and the South Manchuria Railway. The area along the line is rich in products and has very busy freight transportation and is of great economic value. But in fact, it is also a feeder line for the South Manchuria Railway.

(4) Taonan-Ang'angxi Railway (Taoang Road): Starting from Taonan and ending in Ang'angxi, it is 141.7 miles long. Construction started in March of the Republic Year 14 and was completed in July of the Republic Year 15. It was financed by loans from the South Manchuria Railway. This line can compete with the Eastern Railway and absorb goods from the northern part of Eastern Province for export through Dalian. Therefore, the Japanese are extremely willing to invest in construction.

(5) Jinzhou-Fuzhou Line (Jinfu Road): Starting from Jinzhou and ending in Chengzitun, a total length of 63.4 miles. Construction started in May of the Republic Year 15 and was completed in September of the Republic Year 16. It was financed by loans from the South Manchuria Railway of 559,000 yuan. It was built by Chinese and Japanese people.

(6) Tumen-Tieli Road (Tiantu Road): Starting from Difang to Laotougou and from Chaoyangchuan to Juzi Street, it is 69.0 miles long. Construction started in August of the Republic Year 11 and was completed in October of the Republic Year 13. It was jointly operated by Chinese and Japanese officials and merchants. This road is the eastern section of the Ji-Hui Railway and is of utmost importance. Originally, after the Japanese obtained the construction rights of the Ji-Hui Railway in the Tumen River Sino-Korean Boundary Affairs Treaty, they never stopped seeking its realization. However, due to the Chinese people's resolute opposition, there was no way out. After changing their strategy, they did not mention road construction, but instead mentioned mining. They did not use the name of the Japanese government, but the name of Japanese merchants. They did not ask the central government of our country, but asked the Jilin provincial authorities. They began laying tracks to confuse the eyes of the Chinese people. In the middle, there were many negotiations, and it was finally completed. The Japanese's intentions can be imagined. Recently, it was heard that the road has been purchased by the South Manchuria Railway, and negotiations have been completed. If this is true, then the southern section of the Ji-Hui Road has been realized. The situation is extremely critical. What will the Chinese people do?

(7) Benxi-Niuxintai Railway (XiYu Road): Starting from Benxi Lake and ending in Niuxintai, it is 14.7 miles long. Construction started in October of the Republic Year 2 and was completed in February of the Republic Year 3. It was jointly operated by Chinese and Japanese merchants. The purpose of the construction is specifically to transport the coal produced in Niuxintai.

The above-mentioned seven roads, totaling 763.8 miles long, are nominally jointly operated by China and Japan, or owned by our country, but in reality, the power has been lost and is controlled by others. We have no way to intervene. Based on the facts of the past, Japan generally holds two firm central policies on railway loans, namely:

(1) Monopoly on the railway loan rights in the southern part of the Three Eastern Provinces and Jehol. Oppose any third country investing and oppose China building railways with its own funds.

(2) Ensure that all railway loans are borrowed by the South Manchuria Railway Company.

The purpose of this type of railway loan is fourfold. (1) The roads built must be feeder lines for the South Manchuria Railway. (2) Earn interest. (3) Participate in monitoring or interfering with railway management. (4) Establish a hidden line for direct management in the future. The Japanese plan is like this. Learning from past mistakes, the Chinese people should seriously consider this in the future and never fall into their trap again.

(4) Businesses Operated by the South Manchuria Railway Company 64

The South Manchuria Railway Company once stated in its published Manchuria textbook:

"This company bears the mission of developing Manchuria's economy and culture. It aims to develop the health and strength of our citizens (Japanese). It advocates the principle of coexistence and co-prosperity between the two countries (Japan and China) and operates various businesses. In South Manchuria, the emergence of a co-prosperity nation is clearly visible... In addition to the railway transport business, this company also engages in shipping, port management, mining, iron manufacturing, industry, and the development of Manchuria and Mongolia's industries. It also manages various land properties, buildings, artesian wells, and educational facilities within its jurisdiction, and conducts surveys. Although it is named a railway company, it is essentially an executive organ with the functions of a fully-equipped nation." | Manchuria Textbook 210 | 211 pages.

This statement, on the one hand, reveals the arrogance of the Japanese, who disregard our sovereignty and directly regard the development of our Northeast as their responsibility. On the other hand, it further reveals the insidious nature of their methods. They speak of co-prosperity, but in reality, they are developing the health and strength of their own citizens in the "new land of South Manchuria," plundering our treasures, and boasting of their merits in organizing, managing, and properly using them. How can the owner (China) reconcile this? The South Manchuria Railway Company's oppression of our Northeast is no different from the East India Company's oppression of India. It is directly the headquarters of Japan's invasion of our Northeast.

Let us examine the businesses operated by the South Manchuria Railway Company. Besides railway operation as the primary business (including warehouses and factories), it vigorously operates shipping, ports, mining, agriculture, iron manufacturing, electricity, and even hotels, as well as security, education, and surveys. Recently, it has further planned the expansion of iron manufacturing and the operation of oil shale oil production, ammonium sulfate chemical fertilizer, and caustic soda industries, among other major projects. Its influence has deeply penetrated our Northeast, and its roots are firmly established, planting the foundation for Japanese colonization. It is not only alarming but also deeply concerning. The businesses operated by the company are briefly described below:

(1) Railways: The operation of railways has been briefly described above. As for railway ancillary businesses: (A) Warehouse operations. According to 1927 statistics, the incoming goods were 5.24 million tons, and the outgoing goods were 5.28 million tons. The average daily inventory was 340,000 tons. In addition to warehouses, it also provides insurance. (B) Factory operations. These include the Shahekou Factory, Liaoyang Factory, Sujiatun Wood Preservation Plant, and Dalian Electrical Repair Plant. Among them, the Shahekou Factory is the largest in scale, specializing in the manufacturing of locomotives, freight cars, and passenger cars. Currently, there is a tramway between Shahekou and Dalian, which has become a small industrial city.

(2) Shipping: It began operating during the 33rd year of Emperor Guangxu's reign (1907). It has now been transferred to the Dalian Steamship Joint Stock Company and is no longer directly operated. However, the capital of 3 million yuan is entirely owned by the South Manchuria Railway Company. (To be continued)

Important News

Memorial Week for the Central Government and National Government 65

Dai Jitao Reports on the Higher Examination Process

Yu Youren Reports on the Flood Disaster

Central Party Headquarters, August 10, 9 a.m. The Central Party Headquarters held a memorial week for the Premier in the auditorium. Central Committee members Dai Chuanxian, Chen Guofu, Zhu Peide, Ding Weifen, Fang Juehui, Chen Lifu, Yu Jingtang, Miao Peicheng, and staff from various departments and guests, totaling about 500 people, attended. Zhu Peide presided. After the ceremony, Dai Chuanxian reported that he was appointed as the chief examiner for the first Higher Examination. He felt inadequate and apprehensive. Fortunately, the examination committee members diligently and conscientiously performed their duties, striving to avoid errors. After more than ten days in confinement, all matters were completed. On the 9th, the examiners left the confinement simultaneously in the morning. All details of the examination were classified and statistically analyzed, and tables were prepared overnight for clarity. He would now briefly report on the key points: (1) Age: The oldest candidate was 44 years old, and the youngest was 21 years old, with an average age of 28 years and 8 and a half months, a promising age for accomplishment. (2) Native Place: Candidates who passed came from sixteen provinces. The provinces whose candidates did not pass included Shaanxi (8 candidates), Gansu (4), Ningxia and Mongolia (1 each), Rehe and Suiyuan (2 each), Heilongjiang (5), and Yunnan (12). This was due to the small number of candidates from those provinces. (3) Gender: Twenty-two women took the examination, but unfortunately, all failed. It was said that some were quite knowledgeable, which was regrettable. It was probably because women were physically weaker, and the hot weather and continuous rain for several days caused them mental and physical fatigue, preventing them from fully demonstrating their abilities. (4) Party Membership: Among the 43 candidates who passed the general administrative personnel examination, 18 were party members. (5) Qualifications: Ten of the 20 national universities that participated had candidates who passed. Out of 450 candidates, 37 passed. Three of the 18 public universities had candidates who passed. Out of 90 candidates, 3 passed. Two of the 32 private universities had candidates who passed. Out of 630 candidates, 20 passed. One student studying in the United States passed. (6) Experience: Calculated as a percentage, Central University accounted for 16%, Shanghai Jiaotong University 35%, Peking University 5%, Peiping University 4%, Peiping Normal University 23%, and Chaoyang University 3%. The average total score was above 60%. (7) Failures: 44% failed the second test but passed the first test, and 10% failed the first test but passed the second test. The above report was a summary; detailed information would be announced later. The speaker's thoughts on the examination results were: (1) We should strive to improve education to cultivate talent at the root. (2) University graduation examinations should be organized by the government to supplement the national examinations. (3) Examination laws and regulations should be carefully revised to improve academic standards. (4) Equal consideration should be given to examination systems for remote provinces and Mongolia. (5) The government should ensure that those who passed are used to their full potential and not left unused or misused. The meeting adjourned at 10:30 a.m.

National Government. At 10 a.m. on the same day, the National Government held a memorial week for the Premier. Yu Youren, Ma Fuxiang, Li Shuhua, Lian Shenghai, He Yaozu, Liu Ruiheng, Zhu Lihe, Lin Xiang, Ru Yuli, Gao Weiyue, Zheng Hongnian, Zhang Wohua, Chen Shaokuan, and more than 100 staff from the National Government's civil affairs, military affairs, and accounting departments attended. Yu Youren presided. After the ceremony, Yu reported on the flood disaster, saying: "The sages said, 'Yu thought that if there was someone drowning in the world, it was as if he himself were drowning; Ji thought that if there was someone starving in the world, it was as if he himself were starving.' I report on the flood disaster today with this as the theme. Since the beginning of summer this year, there have been many days of heavy rain, and rivers have overflowed. Many cities, towns, and villages have been submerged. The southern and northern provinces and most of the northern regions have become disaster areas. The losses are the worst in decades. The government recognizes this flood disaster as the greatest hidden danger and as something that must be actively addressed. Therefore, it has ordered all provinces to investigate the disaster situation and find ways to provide relief. At the same time, the government believes that the severity of this disaster and the government's failure to plan for flood prevention earlier are reasons for deep self-reproach. However, after this major disaster, the wealthy in various places often take the opportunity to profit, increasing social inequality. Moreover, the disturbances caused by the Red bandits are particularly worrying. Therefore, the government, whether in terms of responsibility or humanitarian sympathy, should be as concerned about the hungry and drowning as Yu and Ji, and strive to provide relief. The society should also fully assist the government and work together to find solutions to overcome the difficulties. At this time, all government colleagues should examine their work and living conditions to see if they are following the Premier's teachings and fulfilling their responsibilities. Only in this way can we face the suffering compatriots. We hope that every organ, every province and county, and every village will have people who are as concerned as Yu and Ji, and not treat this great disaster as something that does not concern them. Then, this great crisis can be overcome." After the report, the ceremony concluded.

Shi Yousan's Resignation Telegram 66

Sent from Dezhou on the 8th

Jinan dispatch: After Shi Yousan's defeat, his troops arrived in Dezhou and were reorganized by Han Fuju. However, there is no confirmed report on Shi Yousan's whereabouts. Today, the military and political organs here received Shi's resignation telegram from Dezhou. The original text is as follows: "To all military and political organs, schools, legal entities, newspapers, and all elders, brothers, sisters, and compatriots throughout the country, Shi Yousan, a humble military man, has served in the army. He dares not claim to be behind others in his heart of saving the country and its people. Therefore, since the Xinhai Revolution, he has participated in almost all domestic wars. Over the past twenty years, politics has become increasingly chaotic, and the powers have increasingly invaded. Those who occupy important positions only know how to seize profits and fight for power, completely disregarding the country's difficulties and the people's hardships. As a result, the vast land of China is about to be destroyed. Yousan, as a soldier, has a responsibility to defend the country and protect the people. Therefore, he has vowed to base his actions on conscience and strive to fight, even at the cost of life and limb, without fear. The past events are all there and can be reviewed. This humble sincerity should be appreciated by the people of the country. Now that his heart is tired and his strength is exhausted, if he were to prolong the war, he would only retire to await the country's worthy men to work together for a good outcome. All of Yousan's troops have been handed over to the two division commanders, Sun Guangqian and Mi Wenhe, to be commanded separately and to join Commander-in-Chief Han Fuju. Since Commander-in-Chief Han and Yousan have shared hardships in the past, entrusting them to his command should prevent any disturbances. Yousan has no regrets in retiring from the military. In his parting words, he cannot express his feelings fully. Whether the country knows him or blames him, it is up to the people. Shi Yousan Qi." (9th)

Chiang's Order

He Jian Strictly Guards Against Guangdong and Guangxi 67

Nanchang dispatch: According to the information released by the Political Training Office of the General Headquarters, the Guangdong-Guangxi invasion plan is divided into four routes. The Guangxi army is concentrated in Quanzhou and Lingsheng. One route advances along the Xiang River from Yongzhou to attack Hengzhou, and the other route advances along the Zi River from Wugang to seize Baoqing. The main force of the Guangdong army is concentrated in Shaoguan, and advances along the Yuehan Railway from Lechang to take Yongxing and Laiyang. Another force advances from Longhuguan into Yongming and Jianghua to spy on Changning. The above four routes focus entirely on the Yuehan Railway and the Xiang River, hoping to join forces in Hengbao in the shortest possible time. The General Headquarters also announced the telegram from the scout in Quanzhou, stating that Chen's rebel army, with fifteen regiments, is advancing towards Longhuguan, and Li's rebel army is advancing towards Lingsheng with twenty regiments. A report from Changsha also stated, "The Xiang-Gui rebel armies have plans to invade Xiang en masse. Li Yangjing has arrived in Lechang. Yan Bogang, a bandit on the Xiang-Yue border, has also been recruited by the Yue army and appointed as the vanguard to disturb Yizhang. Li Pinxian and Qin Yuanfang will soon enter Yong from Quan. Xiang Hanping's troops have also arrived at the Xiang border from Shao. The atmosphere in the counties of southern Xiang is tense. It is heard that Commander-in-Chief Chiang has ordered all armies and He Jian to strictly guard against them." (August 7th)

Higher Examination Unveiling Ceremony Held 68

Lists of Successful Candidates Posted in Front of the Examination Yuan on the 9th

Most Successful Candidates Around 27 or 28 Years Old

Twenty Female Candidates, All Failed

President Dai Expresses Satisfaction with the Results

Beijing News: The various stages of the Higher Examination have been completed in order. The list of successful candidates was first drafted by the Examination Committee. The unveiling ceremony was held on the morning of the 9th. At 9 a.m., Shao Yuanchong, director of the Examination Assistance Office, Wang Yongbin, deputy director, and the supervisory committee members went to the Examination Committee at Nanjing Middle School, Bafutang. Shao Yuanchong personally opened the door, and they entered together to meet the Chief Examiner Dai and the committee members, talking for about ten minutes. Then, they went out together and drove to the Examination Yuan. The car in the lead was decorated with paper flowers, and "Seeking Talents for the Country" was written in front of the car. The list of successful candidates was stored inside, escorted by the two secretaries-general, Chen Daqi and Shen Shiyuan. When the car arrived in front of the Examination Yuan, firecrackers were set off, and military music played. The list was taken out and posted in front of the gate, surrounded by cloth railings, and guarded by police officers to show seriousness. The examination committee members successively entered the reception room of the president's office to rest. Yu Youren, President of the Control Yuan, and Ma Fuxiang, Chairman of the Mongolian and Tibetan Affairs Commission, were waiting in the Yuan and expressed their condolences to Chief Examiner Dai. On this day, Dai wore a blue gauze long gown and a black mandarin jacket. Reporters asked him about his impressions of the Higher Examination. Dai said that the results were satisfactory, thanks to the efforts of the examination committee members, and he was very pleased. However, the examiners were concerned about two things beforehand: one was the province of origin of the successful candidates, and the other was their age. According to the statistics, successful candidates came from sixteen provinces, and the other provinces failed because there were too few candidates. For example, Shanxi had only eight people, Yunnan two, Guangxi five, Gansu two, and Mongolia two. Also, it was inappropriate for the age of the successful candidates to be too old or too young. The average age of the successful candidates this time was around 27 or 28 years old, which was quite appropriate. However, twenty female candidates took the examination, and twelve completed it. It was heard that two of them had a very solid academic foundation. It was initially thought that one or two would pass, but when the list was announced, all the women failed. It was thought that their physical strength and mental energy were not as good as men's, which was regrettable. Dai said at the end that more than twenty kinds of statistical tables in the examination had been ordered to be prepared overnight by the responsible personnel and would be announced by the Examination Assistance Office tomorrow. The efforts of all the staff members in the examination to work hard for the public despite the hot weather were especially commendable. Wuhan Water Levels Rising 69

Wuhan Dikes Continue to Breach

He Chengjun Will Impeach Himself to the Central Government

The Emergency Relief Association is Also Planning Post-Disaster Relief for Various Counties

Hankou communication on the 7th. In Hankou, the city area has been flooded for a week. On the evening of the 6th, there was a heavy downpour, which cleared only on the afternoon of the 7th. The water level rose sharply by more than five inches. Telegrams from Hunan, Chongqing, and Xiangyang successively stated that there was still a water head of more than ten feet or several feet about to reach Hankou, causing panic among the refugees. Even the government authorities were alarmed and at a loss. The dangerous works on the dikes, such as Qiaokou and Huangjingtang in Hankou, the Saihu Dike and Xujiapeng in Wuchang, and the Wutai and Wufeng sluices, have been repaired day and night by Supervisor Xu Yuanquan, Commander Xia Douyin, Director of Water Conservancy Bureau Chen Keming, Mayor of Hankou He Baohua, and Director of Construction Department Fang Dazhi. The dikes have been heightened and thickened. The Saihu Dike is the most dangerous, but it may be safe if the water does not continue to rise. It was originally planned to spend 50,000 yuan to build a dike to drain the accumulated water in Hankou. Construction began on the 7th. The first step is to build a dike starting from Minquan Road, eastward to Jiaotong Road, turning to Yiyuan to Jianghanguan, directly reaching the French Concession. The second step is from the Model District to the railway side, turning to Xunlimen, passing through Laopu, Renshouli, Guanzhongli, Lianbaoli, and Xinhua Company, turning to Laolianbaoli, to reach the Sanchangjie entrance of the Chamber of Commerce, and ending at Minquan Road. First, a soil dike will be built for drainage. The third step will be to continue the drainage. The accumulated water within the area from the Municipal Government to the railway side is scheduled to be completed in five days and will be the responsibility of the Emergency Relief Association. Many refugees have been taken in in recent days. A portion of the refugees along the railway live on the railway embankment, exposed to the scorching sun and rain. The hot and humid conditions have caused many to contract seasonal diseases. In addition to sending doctors to provide medicine, the Association has ordered the refugees to move quickly. Since the refugees are reluctant to leave because they have no place to store their belongings, the Association has specially borrowed the address of the Gongxing Storage and Transportation Company near the railway as a place to store and keep them. At the same time, since the relief funds are too small to be distributed, it has telegraphed the Ministry of Railways, ordering the Pinghan Railway Bureau to add a 5% surcharge to its total revenue for Hubei flood relief for six months, expecting to collect 600,000 yuan to subsidize the civilian food supply. It has also telegraphed various places to relax the ban on grain, and Shanghai and Jiangxi have replied that a large amount of grain will be shipped, which may provide temporary support. According to historical records, this flood is unprecedented. The current Director of the Hubei Water Conservancy Bureau, Chen Keming, the Mayor of Hankou, He Baohua, and the Director of the Pinghan Railway Bureau, Huang Zhenxing, are all responsible. Although Chen and others are trying to shirk their responsibilities, the people have deep resentment. It is not enough to quell public anger without strict investigation. The Provincial and Municipal Party Departments have held several meetings to discuss the matter in detail and will have a very serious response in the coming days. He Chengjun, Director of the Wuhan Provisional Headquarters and Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, is also thoroughly investigating and has reportedly told people that he will impeach himself to the central government.

Hankou communication on the 8th. The water level in Wuhan continues to rise unabated in recent days. According to a telegram from Xiangyang, there is still a water head of 1.6 zhang (approximately 5.3 meters) flowing down the river, causing extreme panic among the people. Flood prevention work has become even more tense. The dikes in the Hankou area, especially the Huangjingtang, Pizijie, and Qiaokou areas, are the most dangerous. The Flood Prevention Office has instructed the Mayor of Hankou, He Baohua, to take charge of the rescue, heightening and thickening the dikes to prevent the Xiang water from continuing to arrive. Sirens will be sounded at night to warn residents to prepare. As of the morning of the 9th, the dike had fortunately not breached. However, one-third of the Donghuajiao Dike under Saijiashan was washed away. The Water Conservancy Bureau and the Municipal Government jointly rescued it. Although there was a small breach, it was immediately blocked, preventing a disaster. As for the breaches in the Jiazhaoji Danshui Pond area, the Flood Prevention Office has sent workers to repair them, and they are generally in order. They will be completed in three to five days. Regarding the drainage of accumulated water, it is also being actively carried out. The street entrances around Hankou City have been temporarily dammed with yellow pine cement, and drainage will begin immediately. However, it is unknown whether the river surface, which is already higher than the banks, can accommodate the huge amount of water. In addition to Wuhan, more than fifty counties in the province have been affected by the flood. There are also some that have not been reported due to poor postal and telecommunications. Refugees are flocking to Hankou, filling every available space. The Emergency Relief Association has telegraphed various places to temporarily prevent refugees from entering the city and has ordered the county magistrates to work with local organizations, just gentry, and citizens to establish emergency relief offices within ten days of receiving the notice to provide relief.

Map of Wuhan Disaster Area 70

Flood Losses in Five Provinces 71

Exceeds 2 Billion Yuan

Nanjing (Central News Agency) - Continuous rainfall since early July, lasting for approximately four weeks, has caused a major flood in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River, the worst in sixty-one years. Rice paddies have been completely washed away, and land transportation to various cities along the river has been almost entirely cut off, relying only on sampans and rowboats to barely maintain traffic. The Yangtze River, one of the world's three major rivers, naturally has a massive volume of water flowing into the sea at all times. However, it is difficult to predict when the accumulated floodwaters in various locations can be expected to recede. The extensive area affected by this flood and the rapid rise of the waters have resulted in significant losses of livestock and human lives. While the exact figures of the current losses are still unclear, a synthesis of various sources indicates that the magnitude is roughly as follows:

Province Flood Area Affected Population Affected Cultivated Land Area Number of Severely Affected Counties

(Square Miles) (Thousands) (Thousands of Mu)

Hubei 18,000 9,000 7,200 30

Hunan 8,500 2,500 3,400 16

Jiangxi 3,500 1,400 1,400 12

Anhui 11,000 5,000 4,400 27

Jiangsu 7,700 5,000 3,000 24

Total 48,700 22,900 19,400

The total number of affected households is approximately 4.5 million, totaling 23 million people. About 10,000 houses have collapsed, and the death toll is in the thousands. The most severe cases include instances in Hubei Province where breaches in the dikes led to entire villages being submerged overnight, resulting in the drowning of most villagers. The area of affected cultivated land accounts for approximately 12% of the total cultivated land area in the country. The areas along the Yangtze River are primarily the best farmlands, so the impact on harvests will exceed 20% of the national harvest. According to elders, it will take at least a year for the current accumulated water to recede. Experts also believe that the water may not completely recede even by the winter's lowest water level. In short, most of this year's autumn harvest is hopeless. In addition, the total direct and indirect losses from agricultural losses, submerged grain storage, and the stagnation of local industries will exceed 2 billion yuan. The National Government plans to issue 10 to 20 million yuan in flood relief bonds to provide assistance.

Tragic Scenes of the Great Flood in Xubu 72

Water Depth Exceeds Four Feet on Level Ground in the City

The Old Course of the Yellow River Rises Again After Rain

Xuzhou Quick Report: Xubu experienced heavy rains last month. The waters of the old course of the Yellow River have risen again due to heavy rainfall upstream, turning the entire town into a swamp. After several days of sunny weather, the water level had dropped. Unexpectedly, one evening, there was a sudden torrential rain that lasted all night. The water flow from the upper reaches of the old course of the Yellow River became even stronger, causing Xubu to return to its original state. Since the first day, the weather has not cleared, with heavy rain falling intermittently. In the lower parts of the city, the water depth reaches the knees. Reports of collapsed houses and deaths have been heard from time to time. As of the 5th, according to a survey by the Construction Bureau, over 160 houses have collapsed, and more than ten people have been killed or injured. The water level in the old course of the Yellow River is only two feet below the bridge deck. On the morning of the 7th, the water from the upper reaches of the old course of the Yellow River suddenly surged down with great force, rising by two feet, causing extreme panic. Unexpectedly, at one o'clock in the afternoon, torrential rain resumed, pouring down for about two hours. The water depth in the level ground of the city reached four feet, and houses in the northwest, northeast, southwest, and southeast corners were completely submerged. Household furniture floated around, traffic was blocked, and floodwaters overflowed. People supporting their wives and carrying their children flocked to higher ground, passing through Zhongshan and Datong Streets, which were free of water, causing congestion. At the same time, the water in the old course of the Yellow River also increased by about a foot. Four arches of the river bridge outside the North Gate were washed away by the rapid current. The Beimalu Bridge outside the East Gate and the Nanmalu Bridge outside the South Gate remain undamaged. However, the Xubu city walls were demolished by the First Division stationed in Xuzhou in 1928. Later, the Education Bureau sold the foundation of the city walls and built houses, completely destroying the city walls. This spring, the embankment of the old course of the Yellow River outside the city was purchased from the Government Property Bureau by the Jiudetang and dismantled, causing the river to overflow and potentially flood the city. The river embankment outside the Xiaobeimen in the northwest of the city has gradually deteriorated over the years, and the terrain is low. River water has flooded outside the gate. The County Government, Construction Bureau, Public Security Bureau, and the First District Office, along with the public, worked overnight to reinforce the embankment and divert the water eastward by digging open a section of the long-distance road from the North Gate to Jiulishan, providing temporary relief. However, the Hexiang mine outside the East Gate was suddenly subjected to a large amount of water from the north, causing waves to surge. The water passed over the East Bridge, damaging one arch of the West End of the South Bridge on the morning of the 8th. The nearby residents gathered at the West End of the river bridge to dig a channel to discharge the water. Although water could be discharged between the North and South bridges, the area near the Huoshen Temple and the Jijui Dam downstream was breached. County and city officials Yang Wei, Qiao Jianming, Liu Zhongxin, Zhu Zhengxue, as well as the heads of various branch bureaus and township chiefs, all supervised the public to repair the breaches at the Huoshen Temple and Jijui Dam. The floodwaters were finally blocked by the afternoon. Over the past two days, approximately 5,000 large and small burlap sacks and rush mats were used in various locations, and four to five thousand people worked with shovels and hoes, united in their efforts to prevent further damage. Fortunately, they were able to preserve the city. However, many of the electric poles in Xubu were also knocked down during the heavy rain. The director of the Telegraph Bureau, Kuang Jingyou, supervised the repair work overnight, ensuring that all four lines were fully operational. This reporter waded through the water this morning to inspect the various locations, which are still being reinforced. The people living along the river are gathered and squatting on the sides of roads and riverbanks, looking extremely miserable. Mr. Guo Hanping, the director of the Xuzhou Xinguang Photography Studio, accompanied by technician Zhu Weinan, inspected and photographed with the reporter team in the rain. It is hoped that kind-hearted people will see this tragic situation and generously provide relief. This is a prayer on behalf of the disaster-stricken people of Xubu. As for the government, the county government reported the disaster to the province on the 6th. The Construction Bureau dispatched technicians to inspect the water situation, measure it daily, and dredge river channels and water gates to provide relief. After the sudden wind and rain on the afternoon of the 7th, while sending people to reinforce the embankment, the county government convened an emergency meeting with representatives from various agencies. County Magistrate Yang Wei presided over the meeting and resolved to (1) organize a Tongshan County Flood Relief Committee; (2) establish an office at the Liquidation Office, which was established immediately; (3) appoint representatives from the county party headquarters, county government, Public Security Bureau, Construction Bureau, Education Bureau, First District Office, Relief Institute, Liquidation Office, Education Association, First and Second District Party Headquarters, Chamber of Commerce, Journalists' Association, Wanzihui, and Farmers' Association as members; (4) mortgage the rice mill to the Bank of China for 10,000 yuan to handle emergency relief. On the afternoon of the 8th, County Magistrate Yang Wei convened a second emergency meeting with representatives from various sectors, deciding to (1) send Li Fengru, Lan Bohua,

Liu Tianzhan, Chen Suyi, etc. to the province to request aid; (2) use the 10,000 yuan mortgaged by the rice mill to first implement price controls; (3) raise funds from various sectors to provide relief. County Magistrate Yang Wei also telegraphed the provincial government on the 6th and 8th to report the disaster and request emergency relief to save the disaster-stricken people. (August 8)

Detailed Report on the Suppression of the Red Army and the Recovery of Xingguo 75

20,000 Bandits Killed, 15,000 Captured

Chiang Awards Meritorious Officers and Soldiers

Nanchang Correspondence: The Battle of Xingguo was the last struggle of the Red Bandits, and it was also the last bloody battle between the Red Bandits and the Suppression Army. Recently, the General Headquarters received a detailed report from the Forward General Headquarters and the Right Wing Commander Chen regarding the progress of the battle. The general gist is: "Last month, Xiang Ying and other bandit groups, numbering tens of thousands, who had fled from Guangchang, Lichuan, and Shicheng in Fujian, planned to return to their old base in southern Jiangxi while our army was attacking Donggu and Ningdu. At that time, our army went straight in and captured Shicheng, cutting off the connection between the Red Bandits in Fujian and Jiangxi. Therefore, there were still about 20,000 bandits hiding in the Ninghua, Tinghang area. As our army successively broke through the bandit nests in various places, the bandits in Fujian detoured through Ruijin and gathered in Xingguo, uniting with scattered bandits who had no nests to return to, numbering no fewer than 30 to 40 thousand. They built solid fortifications in Xingguo, hoping for a final struggle. Our Right Wing Army took advantage of the victory to point south. The 19th Route Army of the First Group attacked Shacun from the southwest of Donggu via Tongqiu, Tianfu, and Wanshi Ridge. Chen Cheng's troops attacked Gupingxu from Zhangzhuang and Caoxi. Zhao Guantao attacked Xingguo City from Quyang Jiecunxu. At the same time, a part of the Left Wing Army came out diagonally from Longkou and Taoxi, heavily surrounding the bandits and launching a joint attack from different directions. Starting on the 30th of last month, a general offensive was launched. Since the bandit army had no way to escape, they had to fight like trapped beasts. Our army advanced step by step, encircling the bandits in the area of Xingguo and Gaoxingxu. Then, the air force was concentrated to bombard them as much as possible. From July 30th to August 4th, over six days, a total of more than 500 120-pound and 160-pound bombs were dropped. The casualties among the bandits were countless. One regiment (the 32nd Regiment) of our Zhao Army bravely advanced directly on the night of the 3rd. By dawn on the 4th, they had forced their way into Xingguo County, fighting fiercely with the bandits on all sides for half a day. As our armies successively arrived, the bandits retreated into the city, closed the city, and defended it firmly. After being bombarded by our air force and artillery for several hours, the city was breached at about 4 o'clock. The officers and soldiers of the regiment swarmed in, fighting the bandits in the streets for several hours, leaving a bloody mess piled up in the streets. Thereupon, the bandits surrendered one after another, and none escaped. It is estimated that about 20,000 bandits were killed in this battle, and more than 15,000 were captured alive. The strength of the bandit forces has been almost completely wiped out. The burying of the bandits' corpses, from the branches to the fish, has not yet been completed." After receiving the telegram, Chiang, in addition to ordering the Ganzhou Party and Government Branch to quickly handle the aftermath, also telegraphed Commander Zhao to quickly restore order and offer condolences to the victims. As for the 32nd Regiment, he sent a telegram commending them and ordering that they be given the rank of Lieutenant Colonel, to be filled as soon as a vacancy arises. In addition, Chiang, with the great merit of suppressing the Red Bandits about to be accomplished, yesterday specially telegraphed He Yingqin and Chen Mingshu to investigate and report the officers and soldiers who had made meritorious contributions, so as to award them. From this, it can be seen that the military campaign to suppress the bandits will soon come to an end. (August 7)

Yangzi Bridge, Jiangdu

Villagers Burn Water Conservancy Bureau's Official Boat 76

And Beat Up the Committee Members and Crew

Water Conservancy Bureau's Official Documents Also Burned

The Zhufang, a ship stationed at the Jiangsu Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau, was intercepted by local people in Yangzi Bridge, Jiangdu County, when it was returning to the province from Gaoyou the day before yesterday (the 8th). The members of the Water Conservancy Bureau, Ouyang Ming, and the crew were beaten up. The ship was dragged to the opposite side of the Gaomin Temple, and burned with kerosene and firewood. In addition, six boxes of official documents from the Gaoyou Water Conservancy Bureau over the years were burned and destroyed. In addition to those who were injured, several government officials and crew members are missing. The Construction Department's Water Conservancy Bureau and the Shipping Association have sent people to Jiangdu County to investigate. The details of the incident are listed below:

Cause of the Incident: Over the years, when the Grand Canal's water level rises, the Yangzi Bridge water mark exceeds 12 feet 4 inches, the boats between Guazhou and Yangzi Bridge must be towed and stop. When steamers happen to pass by, a small number of busybodies gather people under the pretext of protecting the dam and detain the boats to pursue their own interests. According to people in the shipping industry, disputes have occurred frequently in recent years. For example, in 1929, the Fengshun and Hengtong were detained in Yangzi Bridge, and the crew members were beaten and the objects were damaged. In 1930, the Henggui and Yuanchang were detained in Liuqian, and they were allowed to leave only after mediation. Last month, the Jiangsu and Fengshun were detained again in Yangzi Bridge. They were only released after the township head and deputy set conditions. It can be seen from this that the local people have malicious behaviors toward merchant ships and official boats passing by.

The Circumstances of the Trip: The Zhufang small steamer was funded by the Zhenjiang Fuhua Company and purchased from the Lisu Company for use by the Shipping Affairs Office. This trip was made after the Water Conservancy Bureau sent a letter to the Shipping Association requesting a loan from the Office. On the 6th, more than 7,000 burlap sacks were loaded, and at dawn on the 7th, they set off to Gaoyou to provide emergency damming work. On the 8th, Ouyang Ming, a technician from the Water Conservancy Bureau, was sent back to the province to report on the water situation and the dike project, with six boxes of documents attached. They set off southward at 2 PM.

Beating People and Burning Boats: At about 6 PM that afternoon, when the Zhufang steamer was passing the north end of Yangzi Bridge, Jiangdu County, someone beat a gong to gather people and shouted for the boat to stop. The helmsman heard the sound and dared not move forward. The rioters then boarded several boats and crossed the center of the river. Some people dove into the water and rushed onto the Zhufang steamer to smash objects and beat people indiscriminately. At that time, Committee Member Ouyang held up the official documents and stated that this boat was an official boat for the Water Conservancy Bureau. The rioters not only ignored him, but also kidnapped and took Committee Member Ouyang, the captain, and the boatmen ashore, and beat them severely. They then let the Zhufang steamer drift to the opposite side of Gaomin Temple, poured kerosene on the boat, and then burned it with reeds until the boat sank to the bottom of the water. Only a few inches of the chimney were visible on the water surface.

Injuries: Ouyang Ming, a technician from the Engineering Department of the Water Conservancy Bureau, was originally a weak scholar. After being beaten, he had many wounds all over his body, and the blood on his arm was blurred. He was unconscious for a long time during the beating before waking up. He was then detained at the local sub-station. At 9 PM that night, he was sent to the Dandu County government. Captain Zou Hanquan of the boat was also beaten. The apprentice Xiao Cunzi and others were treated at the Provincial Hospital. Other injuries, both minor and severe, have not yet been investigated thoroughly.

Shipping Association Report: Jiang Zaishan, the old purser of the Zhufang, escaped back to the office and reported the situation. Then, the Zhenjiang Shipping Association telegraphed the Water Conservancy Bureau on his behalf. The telegram read: "To the Director and other members of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Conservancy Bureau: According to a telegram from the Shipping Affairs Office, Jiang Zaishan, the purser of the Zhufang, reported this morning that the Zhufang small steamer was rented by the Water Conservancy Bureau through the Shipping Affairs Office on the 6th, loaded with more than 7,000 burlap sacks, and sent to Gaoyou to provide emergency damming work, flying the flag of the Water Conservancy Bureau. The boat left Zhenjiang at dawn on the 7th and returned to the province at the request of Committee Member Ouyang of the Water Conservancy Bureau after completing the public affairs in Gaoyou. At about 1 PM on the 8th, it set off southward. At 6 PM, when passing Yangzi Bridge, someone beat a gong to gather people and shouted for the boat to stop. The helmsman heard the sound and docked the boat. When Mr. Ouyang held up the official documents and stated that it was the official boat of the Water Conservancy Bureau, three or four people suddenly shouted and started beating. Then, a large number of people swarmed onto the boat, beating the committee member and the crew. They then went ashore and tied up many people, and then let the boat drift to the opposite side of Gaomin Temple, where they burned the boat completely with kerosene and rice straw until it sank in the water. There were also six boxes of documents from the Water Conservancy Bureau in the boat, which were burned as well. Zaishan and others fled into the water in a hurry. Xiao Sanzi, Gu Xueyi, and Xie Yongshi were injured, and Zaishan, Zhu Taozi, and Chen Mazi escaped. The remaining crew members, Captain Zou Hanquan, Second Mate Xu Xiaolin, sailor Xiao Liu, cook Xiao Heshang, and apprentice Xiao Cunzi, are currently missing. Therefore, in addition to sending the injured to the Provincial Hospital for treatment, we will submit a further report on the details. We hereby send a telegram in advance, and we pray that the honorable office will quickly send people to the site to investigate with the personnel of our association and the office staff so that relief can be handled.

Songjiang 77

News of the Arrest of Bandits in Fengjing and Jinshanwei: Ma Anfu, an intelligence agent of the Songhu Pacification Division, recently received a report that three suspected bandits, He Jinyun, He Longshan, also known as Ah Hang, were hiding in the countryside of Fengjing. He immediately went to the address to investigate and arrest them. They were bound and escorted to the 5th Company headquarters of the 2nd Battalion of the 2nd Security Regiment stationed in Jinze for detention. On the 5th of this month, he was hiding at the Yue family in Xiyue, Jinshanwei. Fang, the battalion commander stationed in Jinshanwei, found out about it and sent a team to search. Wu the Bandit hid in the flower field and escaped. The troops fired their guns in pursuit, but there was no trace of him. They brought the bandit's wife, father-in-law, and brother-in-law, a total of three people, back to the battalion headquarters for custody.

The Contact for the Ransom of Kidnapped Bandits is Captured: The 12th Team of the 3rd District of the Water Police captured Jiang Xintian, a bandit who was contacting the ransom of a kidnapped person, on the shore of Yangcheng Lake the other day (the 9th). He was escorted to the District Headquarters on the 10th. Wujiang 80

Business Tax Collection in This County: The business tax in this county, except for the towns of Shengze and Zhenze, is handled by the Wujiang County Chamber of Commerce with the approval of the Finance Department. The tax payment for the fourth, fifth, and sixth months has been paid in advance. The Chamber of Commerce began collecting it earlier this morning. Due to the continuous rain and the rapid rise of the river, traffic was cut off, delaying the start of the collection. Now, because of repeated urging from the Provincial Department, it has been decided to start collecting on the 10th of this month, and the Farmers' Bank in the city will be used as the collection office.

Robbery Occurs in Guajing Port: Guajing Port, seven miles away from the city, is a place where bandits appear and disappear. At 11 AM yesterday (the 8th), a bandit boat suddenly docked there. There were four bandits on the boat, two with pistols and two unarmed. Seeing three express boats from Suzhou to various towns, they shouted for the boats to stop one after another. Three bandits entered the boats to rob, and one bandit kept watch. All the silver dollars and clothes of the passengers on the boats were robbed. After the robbery, the bandits got off the boat and set sail to Taihu Lake. The passengers on these three boats suffered heavy losses. Recently, because the river has not receded and the steamers have stopped running, the passengers on the boats are all from the business and academic circles. After the robbery, the three boats reported to the Wujiang Land and Water Police Team to strictly arrest the bandits and ensure the safety of travelers.

Wuxi 81

Tragic Accident of House Collapse at Zhongdong Theater: The Zhongdong Theater outside Guangfu Gate was funded by local people such as Xu Guofeng and Yao Ganshi. The house was contracted by a Guo from Jiangyin, and the workmanship and materials were shoddy. The Construction Bureau ordered improvements, but they were able to dredge it and start drumming peacefully. At first, they screened movies, and then changed to southern opera. At about 9 PM the other night, when Chen Cai'e was singing the second act of The Pearl Pagoda when the neighbor Wang's house (ie, the house of Caiyun, the famous Zhuangzhu of Hanzhuang, which was destroyed by fire a few months ago) suddenly collapsed. At the same time, six frames of the Zhongdong house also collapsed, and the viewers who were close to it were pressed inside. For a time, calling men to find women, losing earrings and shoes, I don't know how many. As a result, forty people were sent to the hospital, including Wang Arong, Ni Jingen, Du Zhu, and Du Qizhen, a six-year-old girl, who were seriously injured and their lives were in danger. When the accident happened, the order was chaotic, and the traffic was blocked one after another. The police of the Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau were sent to the scene to suppress the situation. Li Kun, the manager of the hospital, knew that he could not escape the responsibility and had already fled without a trace.

Please Punish the Judge in the Bone Steaming Examination Case: Gong, the wife of Li Zhilin, a villager in Yangshuyuan Township of the County, was beaten to death during her lifetime and her body was abandoned in the river. Zhu Zonghai, the prosecutor of the County Court, initially found no injuries after the examination. Gong Gengtang, the father of the deceased, refused to accept and reported to the High Court to send another examiner to Wuxi to open the coffin for steaming examination. The scars were numerous, and the chief prosecutor Zhou Erkai re-examined and clarified. The murderer Li Zhilin was immediately taken into custody. Afterwards, the family of the deceased Gong Gengtang filed a suit with the High Court, requesting that Zhu Zonghai, the prosecutor of the case, and Shen Zemin, the examiner, be punished for the crime of embezzlement and perversion of justice, and that they be dealt with severely. The Wuxi County Court's chief prosecutor, Zhou Erkai, was ordered to investigate and verify the matter. Zhou Chuxi has dismissed Shen Zemin, and Zhu Zonghai has also been ordered to be transferred to other places. Huang Jie has been appointed by the High Court to fill the vacancy.

Jiangsu Province's Expanded Publicity on the Prevention and Elimination of Silkworm Diseases: In order to arouse silkworm farmers' efforts to prevent and eliminate silkworm diseases, the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Agriculture and Mines has organized the Jiangsu Provincial Silkworm Disease Prevention and Elimination Propaganda Association, which is divided into provincial propaganda associations and county propaganda associations. The Provincial Propaganda Association is jointly organized by the Department of Agriculture and Mines and the Provincial Silkworm Experiment Field, Silkworm Industry Supervision Office, Provincial Seed Manufacturing Office, and other agencies. It has been decided to be held in Wuxi on August 10, and the Tonggeng Hall and Wuxi Grand Theater in the park will be designated as the meeting places. The various silkworm industry agencies have sent their products to the meeting for display, making large-scale publicity.

Yangzhou 83

Summary of County Government Meeting: At 9:00 AM on the 8th, the county government held a county government meeting, chaired by the county head. The most important items on the agenda were: (1) To establish a branch office for measurement and standardization verification, starting with a third-class facility, with monthly expenses of 250 yuan. In addition to allocating verification fees, the shortfall will be covered by the finance bureau using local reserve funds, to be reimbursed upon securing funds. The county will submit this to the provincial authorities for approval. (2) The construction bureau submitted a cost estimate for repairing the city wall atop Tianning Gate. It was decided that the construction bureau should estimate the repair costs for all city gates and walls, and a verified report will be submitted for further review. (3) The Fourth District Office submitted temporary regulations for public ferries at Wantou. It was decided that the construction bureau should expedite the establishment of ferry services, eliminating the need for private boats. Before the ferry service is operational, the construction bureau will, in conjunction with the local public safety bureau, strictly prohibit small boats from carrying passengers.

Annual Business Tax Package of 40,000 Yuan: The Jiangdu business tax has been negotiated by Wang Jingting, chairman of the chamber of commerce, with the provincial authorities to an annual package of 40,000 yuan, payable in quarterly installments. Both parties have signed a contract, and the business tax bureau will be abolished on the 10th, with an office established instead, attached to the chamber of commerce. The collection method for the package will be decided by the chamber of commerce in consultation with the town chambers of commerce and industry associations, and a contract will be mutually agreed upon. Teng Yizhai and Ling Gengbo have been appointed as reviewers to facilitate the process.

Hangzhou 84

Bus on Gongsanduan Highway Shot at Midway: At 7:30 PM on the 9th, bus No. 64 on the Gongsanduan Highway in Hangzhou, on its last trip carrying passengers from Sanlangmiao back to the Xidajie repair shop, was passing near Fengshan Gate. The area was quiet and sparsely populated. In the dim evening light, a gunshot was suddenly heard. A bullet flew through the front windshield. Fortunately, the bus was traveling quickly, and no one was injured, but the passengers were pale and panicked. At that time, only a few people resembling soldiers were seen passing by on the road. The driver quickly accelerated and sped away, avoiding a potential disaster.

Hurricane Hits Hangzhou Yesterday: Hangzhou has been experiencing sweltering weather for days, with no relief even after the start of autumn. On the morning of the 10th, a hurricane suddenly swept through, blowing in from the northwest. It intensified at 1:00 PM. More than ten utility poles along Xidajie in the city were blown down, disrupting traffic. Public buses were rerouted via Wutang Road and Zhaoqingsi Temple. Yellow sand obscured the roads, and several thatched sheds in Songmuchang and other places were blown down. The storm showed no sign of abating until 5:00 PM.

Xiaoshan 85

Accident on Xiaoshao Highway in Qianqing: Passenger bus No. 51 on the Xiaoshao section of the highway, departing from Wuyunmen on the morning of the 7th, was traveling along the riverbank to the vicinity of Qianqing when an elderly woman was walking along the road. The driver tried to avoid her and braked, but due to the high speed, the sudden stop caused the bus to overturn. Nine passengers were injured, the most seriously injured being Ding Zhimei (from Ruanshe, manager of Xiguo Yutai Rice Store). The injured were taken to Xiaoshan Jianming Hospital for treatment. Two Bandits Arrested in Dayi Kidnapping Case: Wang Guisheng, a villager from Dayi in eastern Xiaoshan, was kidnapped by bandits on the 23rd of last month. Wang's family received as many as ten letters from the bandits, demanding a ransom of 52,000 yuan. The last letter instructed Wang's family to send someone to book a room at the Juelu Hotel in Shanghai on August 4th, holding a hatbox from Zhang Yunsheng Hat Shop in Hangzhou as a signal. Someone would contact them. Wang followed the instructions and successfully apprehended Chen Xuewen and Zhou Luren. They have been sent to Hangzhou by the Shanghai police for legal proceedings. Meanwhile, three suspected accomplices have been arrested in Xiaoshan.

County Head to Wuxi to Study Papermaking: Many residents in the southern part of Xiaoshan make a living by papermaking. The annual output is quite large, but in recent years, there has been no improvement, leading to failures. County Head Du once initiated the establishment of the Lida Paper Mill and is already preparing and starting to raise shares. He has also submitted a request to the province for approval. County Head Du believes that the products of the Wuxi paper mill are of excellent quality, so he plans to depart immediately for Wuxi to study papermaking, hoping to learn from their experience.

Education News

Important News 86

Shaanxi Education Department to Examine Middle School Teachers 87

Examination to be Held on August 12th

Qualified Candidates Will Be Recommended by the Department for Employment

The "Provisional Regulations on the Qualifications, Appointment, Dismissal, and Treatment of Teaching Staff in Shaanxi Provincial Secondary Schools" has been passed by the Shaanxi Provincial Government's administrative meeting. Regarding teacher qualifications, those who have not graduated from domestic or foreign universities, or who have not studied at a school, may also be employed, but they must be examined by the Education Department. In order to carefully select teachers, the department has specifically established "Regulations for the Examination of Teachers in Shaanxi Provincial Secondary Schools." Anyone who meets the examination qualifications and aspires to be a teacher, regardless of whether they have been invited by various schools, must register with the department and await examination according to the examination regulations. Those who pass the examination will be issued a certificate by the department and recommended to various schools for employment. The regulations are attached below:

Regulations for the Examination of Teachers in Shaanxi Provincial Secondary Schools: A. Qualifications: (1) Studied at a domestic or foreign university for more than two years and served as a middle school teacher for more than two years; (2) Served as a middle school teacher for more than three years; (3) Has a definite research and published work on specialized academic subjects; (4) Graduates of domestic or foreign universities or specialized schools that have not been established or recognized by the Ministry of Education. B. Examination Subjects: Chinese Language, History and Geography, English, Physics and Chemistry, Mathematics, Natural History, Drawing, Music. C. Examination Committee: Li Xie, Li Bailing, Jing Zhiyi, Lian Ruiqi, Wang Ruoxi. D. Registration Essentials: (1) Registration is open from now until August 10th at the Education Department; (2) Must submit service certificates, academic works, published works, or graduation certificates. Those whose academic works or published works are deemed qualified after review will be exempt from the examination; (3) Candidates may choose one or more of the examination subjects. E. Examination Date: Starting from August 12th at the Education Department.

Jinan University

New Marine Specimen Collection by the Department of Biology 94

Collected Over 500 Species from Fourteen Districts

Li Guochang, chairman of the Department of Biology at the College of Science of National Jinan University, and teaching assistant Huang Nong, were invited by the Chinese Society of Marine Products to attend research activities in Xiamen. Li researched lancelets, and Huang researched seabirds. President Zheng of the university entrusted them to collect marine specimens in Macau, Hong Kong, Xiamen, and Fuzhou. The work has now been completed, and they returned to the school yesterday. It is reported that they collected specimens in Nanwan, Xiangzhou Bay, Shau Kei Wan, Gulangyu, Meihua, Sandu, and other fourteen districts, totaling over five hundred species of fish, shrimp, crabs, clams, echinoderms, mollusks, and coelenterates, packed into several large boxes, including many rare specimens.

End of Shanghai Summer School 96

The fourth session of the summer school at Shanghai Middle School in Nanshi, Shanghai Province, has been effective since its opening. The eagerness of students to study and the progress of the school have been remarkable. The school ended yesterday. The closing ceremony was held at 8:00 AM, chaired by director Shen Yizhen. In addition to reporting on the overall situation of the summer school for the past five weeks, he encouraged students to pay attention to their academic studies, physical training, and character cultivation. His words were extremely sincere. Next, Dr. Cha Fangji, a guest speaker, gave a speech on "Impressions After Traveling to the United States," encouraging students to focus on scientific research and promote the spirit of democracy. Everyone was moved. Finally, certificates of completion and prizes for essays and exams were awarded. The meeting adjourned at around 10:00 AM.

New Contribution to Sports: Ma Detai's "Tennis Training Method" Published 109

China's First Tennis Book

Published by Shanghai Qinfen Bookstore

Essential Reading for Tennis Lovers

In recent years, the sport of tennis has become extremely popular among Chinese people. Tennis competitions have sprung up like mushrooms after rain, and the sound of tennis matches is constantly heard. This is a very good phenomenon, as tennis is suitable for people of all ages, regardless of gender, and there is no seasonal restriction. It is beneficial to health and is a very beneficial sport. However, although there are many enthusiasts and diligent practitioners, progress in technique is difficult to achieve due to a lack of learning methods and good guidance. This is a great regret. Shanghai Qinfen Bookstore, in view of this, and with the aim of promoting sports and making up for the above-mentioned shortcomings, has recently invited Ma Detai, the former tennis instructor of the National Games, to write the book "Tennis Training Method." The content is excellent and complete, divided into ten chapters: Chapter 1: Introduction; Chapter 2: Grip Method; Chapter 3: Hitting Method; Chapter 4: Singles Competition Method; Chapter 5: Doubles Competition Method; Chapter 6: Key Points During Competition; Chapter 7: Attitude During Competition; Chapter 8: Key Points During Player Training; Chapter 9: On-Court Strategy; Chapter 10: Secrets to Winning. The entire book provides detailed and clear instructions on tennis hitting techniques, training methods, etc., without leaving anything unsaid. Each chapter also includes correct posture demonstrations, with photos taken by tennis players Yu Tianguang and others, printed on high-quality copperplate paper, which are exceptionally clear. The special feature of this book is that it integrates the strengths of Europe and the United States, takes into account the situation in China, and is written as a special book suitable for Chinese training, which is commendable. The author, Mr. Ma, has served as the instructor of the Chinese tennis team at the 7th, 8th, and 9th Far Eastern Games, so he has rich experience in tennis and has his own unique insights. His writings are based on scientific methods as the basis for training. Therefore, this book is the most suitable tennis book for China and should be the first tennis book in the country. It is a new contribution to the sports world. The hardcover book is priced at five jiao, with a special price of nine discounts, four jiao and five fen, and postage of eight fen. The general distributor is Qinfen Bookstore, No. 39 Xinmin Village, Malang Road, Shanghai. The Shanghai consignment points are the Chinese National Sports Association on Laoxinfu Road, the World Bookstore on Sima Road, the Datong Bookstore, the Qixin Bookstore on Qipan Street, the Wenming Bookstore on Nanjing Road, the Huadong Sports Equipment Company on Central Road, the Qianghua Company on Sichuan Road, Lianchangji Tennis Racket Shop, the Standard Sports Company in Ximen, the City First Stadium, and major bookstores in various ports.
