Free Talk

World Anecdotes 180

— Hai Ke

Husband Famine

During the Great War, Britain suffered significant losses of soldiers, leading to a sharp decline in the male population domestically. This has made it difficult for women to find husbands, resulting in a "husband famine" phenomenon. According to recent surveys, an unusually large number of British women between the ages of thirty and fifty are living single lives due to the inability to find husbands, breaking previous records.

Hot Air Instead of Towels

In Paris, France, a restroom in a train station has been equipped with a device that emits hot air for drying hands after washing. Instead of using towels, one simply holds their wet hands up to the device, and they will dry in seconds. This is much more convenient than wiping with towels, and the train station can save a significant amount of money each year on purchasing towels.

Palm House

The London Zoo is one of the most famous zoos in the world. Its extensive collection and comprehensive facilities are unmatched by other zoos. Within the zoo is a special palm house, where the temperature is exactly like that of the tropics. Delicate monkeys and wading birds that originate from tropical regions are kept here, so they can live as if they were still in the tropics.

Kang Nanhai's Seal 181

— Surviving Swords and Arrows

Mr. Kang Youwei was a man from Nanhai County. His original name was Zu Yi. When he participated in the imperial examinations, over six thousand candidates submitted a memorial to the emperor. Kang Youwei took the lead. After gaining official status, he observed that Emperor Dezong was controlled internally by his mother (Empress Dowager Cixi) and externally by powerful traitors. He then sought to implement new policies and purge the court of these treacherous officials. Although he rose in rank through his position as a bureaucrat, he still enjoyed imperial favor. Liang Qichao was a disciple of Kang, and they were both part of the reformist faction. However, their views diverged significantly. Opponents fabricated rumors, claiming that Kang presented red pills to the emperor, clouding his judgment. A political purge ensued, and Kang fled into exile. At that time, a friend presented him with a couplet: "How can there be the poisoner Yang Shuzi, regretting the absence of Cao Zhi; hating the lack of a drafted indictment like Luo Binwang." After the Republic of China was established, Kang returned to the country. In the spring of the second year, when the National Assembly was drafting a constitution, Kang repeatedly requested that Confucianism be established as the state religion, but to no avail. He then went to Xuzhou to meet with Zhang Xun, asking for his assistance. Xun, respecting Kang's character, sent a telegram of support, and the phrase "Confucianism as the state religion" was added to the article on religious freedom. Although this proposal has now been revoked, one cannot help but admire his dedication to promoting sacred learning. Before the restoration attempt, Kang arrived in Beijing and shielded himself with a large palm-leaf fan as he left the train, drawing much criticism. Shortly after, Kang became the president of the Bide Yuan (Office of the President) but resigned after only a few days. He has not held any official positions since. From this, we can see that although Kang was committed to reform, he was not aligned with the revolution. Mr. Kang's writing style was naturally unrestrained, and his calligraphy was elegant and refined. When he came to Xuzhou, I happened to be working as a scribe in the Seventh Route Command Headquarters. I requested that he write a楹聯 (楹聯 yínglián, a pair of scrolls with antithetical sentences displayed vertically) for me, and he stamped it with a large seal, inscribed with the lines: "One hundred days of reform, thirteen years in exile, traveled thirty-two countries, walked four hundred thousand miles." Such a seal is unprecedented and can be said to belong to one of the most talented figures of the late Qing Dynasty.

Ode to the Moon After a Long Rain 182

— He Tianjian

After more than twenty days of wind and rain, the damp clouds suddenly dispersed one day, revealing the bright moon. Wealthy guests set up wine, while disaster victims await food. They both look at the moon, but their joys and sorrows are different. Moved by this, I composed this poem.

Damp clouds have surrounded my house for over twenty days,

Living in seclusion, as if sleeping at the bottom of a well.

The moss is green and thick on all four walls,

Even the snails stretch out their horns and go crazy.

North and south of the great river, the crops are in peril,

East and west of the fields, the water connects endlessly.

The old farmers look up at the roof, sighing helplessly,

Leaving only the empty chapters of Shanfu's water management.

Tonight, I suddenly hear the sound of rain cease,

Outside the window, the dark clouds are swept away by the wind.

In an instant, the clouds disperse, and the moon's disc emerges,

Like a lovely woman applying makeup in the morning.

The clouds are like chaotic clusters embracing the pear blossom face,

Obscuring the moth eyebrows, making them incredibly pitiful.

Suddenly, a cloud mass comes from the east,

Resembling a venomous dragon crouching in the Big Dipper constellation.

The light shoots from its head, its momentum abruptly rising,

Ferociously pouncing on the icy wheel, swallowing it whole.

It is as if the beauty returned to Zhili,

Frustration fills my heart, impossible to express.

I only see the remaining radiance shooting in all directions,

Like silk threads, like strands, and like fists.

The Wind Goddess suddenly scolds A Xiang to leave,

And the monstrous clouds begin to release the rotating Chang'e.

It is like Wenji returning to the Han people,

Like a dark pearl emerging from the deep abyss.

The clear shadow is admired by all nations together,

But the disaster victims are left to linger on their last breaths.

North and south of the house, white waves float,

Perhaps there are beams washed away without a single tile remaining.

What are my feelings when I look up at the moon at this time?

I only feel sorrow and sob.

What is the intention of those who set up wine in the grand hall?

They spare no expense on delicacies and rare dishes.

The Yue maidens and Wu girls lean against each other, drunk.

Passersby look at them as if they were gods.

How happy are they to look at the moon at this moment?

They are free from all earthly constraints.

Alas, we all look at the same bright moon,

But our joys and sorrows are as different as heaven and earth.

I, too, hesitate and cannot bear to look,

Let the bright spirit be round outside the window.

Talking About Miniature Golf 183

— Yu Gong

In June of last year, a new fad suddenly emerged in the United States – miniature golf – and it quickly swept across the country. Now it has become popular in Shanghai, becoming one of the most fashionable forms of entertainment. Now, I will talk casually about everything about miniature golf.

The Origin of Miniature Golf: Initially, a Mr. Thomson from Mexico and a Mr. Albert from Texas, USA, wanted to play golf. However, the soil in Mexico and Texas contained too much sand, making it unsuitable for golf. They had no choice but to create a rudimentary form of golf to satisfy their craving. They used artificial means to create some mud and grass and added some artificial hills and small bodies of water, playing in the courtyard. Later, some people felt there was an opportunity to be seized, so they greatly embellished it and innovated the designs. The American temperament has always been to follow the crowd, and one person's singing is met with a hundred voices in harmony. Thus, miniature golf became a new fad.

The Reasons for the Development of Miniature Golf: Big golf is expensive and time-consuming. Only wealthy sons and gentlemen have the money and time to play. The average American goes to work early in the morning and doesn't return until five in the afternoon. After a short rest, it is already late. Naturally, they don't have time to play. Miniature golf can be played indoors, regardless of day or night, and it is not affected by wind or rain. It also doesn't take much time. No wonder everyone is flocking to it.

The Situation of Miniature Golf in the United States: According to a survey in August of last year, there were 25,000 miniature golf courses in the United States. The equipment cost for each course was approximately $5,000, with a total investment of $125 million. The average revenue for each course is $200 per day. That means the capital is earned back after one month. Many companies specialize in building artificial golf courses for people's homes, with each piece ranging from $12 to $50. Many young people prefer playing miniature golf to going to the movies. Therefore, some movie theaters with sluggish business have been converted into miniature golf courses. Some large shipping companies have also added this entertainment option to attract passengers.

The Miniature Golf Fever in Shanghai: Since miniature golf flowed into Shanghai from the United States, everyone is vying to imitate it. Playing miniature golf has also become one of the conditions of being modern. There is one course in Shanghai's western district that uses electricity to control caves and bridges. The cave doors open and close, and the drawbridges are raised and lowered. You have to hit the ball when the cave door is open and the drawbridge is down to pass. Although it is more difficult, it is very interesting and can be considered a novel approach.

A Visit to Buddhist Doctor Hu 184

— Fei Tang Xueqing

The traditional Chinese medicine doctor Hu Tianxiang, styled Fo, hails from Wuling. He possessed extraordinary intelligence from a young age and could recite anything after seeing it once. He enjoyed studying Buddhist principles and was diligent and tireless. His footprints have practically covered all the major temples in the country. He received the art of medicine from a remarkable person. His prescriptions were effective against ailments. In his prime, he traveled to Shanghai and settled there. Wang Yiting, a prominent figure in Shanghai, admired his reputation and invited him to discuss Chan Buddhism. Hu's words contained profound Chan principles, which greatly impressed Wang. Wang is also a steadfast supporter of Buddhism.

Hu is not only skilled in pulse diagnosis and deeply versed in Buddhism, but he also excels in poetry. At the fiftieth anniversary celebration of Yu Qiaqing, I witnessed a hanging scroll personally written and calligraphed by Hu. Both the writing and calligraphy were exquisite and possessed a unique style. My son, Manqian, suffered from stage II tuberculosis. He consulted Hu, and within ten days, his condition improved from severe to mild, and then to complete recovery. Recently, Xiaoqian fell ill again. As a three-year-old toddler who is just learning to speak, it was difficult to ascertain his condition. Therefore, I accompanied him to Hu's residence on Xiangshan Road in Zhabei to seek treatment. This was my first visit to Hu. Upon entering the room, I saw that the four walls were adorned with a dazzling array of books and paintings. The Buddhist statues on the central table were all masterpieces by famous artists. Hu was humble, courteous, and emphasized that patients should eat vegetarian food because vegetables are rich in nutrients, which are incomparable to meat. Moreover, during the summer months, if one can avoid meat and eat vegetarian food, one can avoid all seasonal illnesses. I have been a vegetarian for ten years and have never suffered from minor illnesses. This is the reason. As for Mr. Fei's illness, he should chant "Amitabha Buddha" more often. This is because his illness is caused by excessive mental exertion and neurasthenia. Those who engage in writing often rack their brains and are prone to this condition. If one chants the Buddha's name more often, one will only know Buddha in their mind's eye and nothing else, which can avoid many worries. His illness will not be difficult to cure suddenly. Many people say that I believe in Buddha and make others believe in Buddha. This is actually a misunderstanding of my views. I heard these words and affirmed them again and again. I thanked him with Xiaoqian and left. (He did not accept any payment.)

Brief News: Recently, someone in Hankou has raised a large amount of capital to establish a department store called Xinhua Company. It will be no less than Sincere & Co. and Wing On in Shanghai. Inside, there will be a Lingxiao Amusement Park, which will be grand in scale and filled with a variety of performances. Recently, special representatives Yao Youbang and Li Feishu have been sent to Shanghai to invite performers. All the famous performers in Shanghai are being recruited. It is said that the grand opening will be on August 1st of the lunar calendar.

Publishing News: The "Three-Day Children's Pictorial" is an excellent reading material for children. Its various advantages have been detailed in an article by Mr. Sheng Han specifically for children's newspapers. The annual subscription price is 1.90 yuan, including postage, and the half-year subscription price is 1 yuan, including postage. The subscription address is: "Children's Times Publishing House, No. 11 Xiaoxiaochang, Shaoxing, Zhejiang."

Rotary Club of "Say Book"

Women, Women (16) 186

— Yao Su Feng

After dropping off the guest at the station, he didn't take any other business and pulled the rickshaw home. The young apprentice kept chattering about Xiao Rong, insisting that he hadn't mistaken anyone. He talked so much that Xiao Rong's father finally couldn't help but believe him, and he could only sigh deeply.

When he got home, he told his family about it. Xiao Rong's wife finally remembered and said, "Father, it must be Xiao Rong! I saw him at the station too, with a woman. But I was confused at the time and thought I was mistaken, so I let it go. Now, hearing what the apprentice said, everything is clear." She almost cried as she spoke.

"Could it really be Xiao Rong? He only left the day before yesterday. How could he be back today, and with a beautiful woman? Who is she? Who is she? I think maybe it's not really Xiao Rong," Xiao Rong's mother said, still somewhat doubtful.

"How could it not be Xiao Rong! He even spoke to me!" the apprentice said.

Xiao Rong's father was really angry. By this time, he also believed that the person sitting in his rickshaw just now was Xiao Rong. So he told the apprentice to hurry to the railway hotel and call Xiao Rong home.

The apprentice obeyed the order and went. When he got to the railway hotel, he first looked at the water sign but couldn't find the name Lu Xiao Rong. He had to ask the cashier and the people inside, "A man and a woman, who came from Shanghai today, in which room are they?" he asked.

"What a joke! There are so many men and women from Shanghai! How do I know which one you're looking for? What's the surname? What's the name?" the cashier said with a smile.

"The surname is Lu, the name is Xiao Rong!" the apprentice only knew this much.

"There isn't one! There are no guests with the surname Lu today!" the cashier replied, glancing roughly at the register.

The apprentice had no choice but to go back and report. The whole family could only feel puzzled and had no idea what to do. Later, Xiao Rong's mother came up with an idea. She told the apprentice to get up early the next morning and wait at the entrance of the railway hotel. Since he was staying inside, he would definitely come out. When he came out, he could pull him home.

A New Atmosphere of Calm in the Money Market 191

Market Overview: Yesterday was Monday. Banks were open, and the financial market atmosphere was generally better than usual. Furthermore, the money shops were particularly busy with settlements due every ten days. All kinds of procedures were exceptionally busy, and the combination of these two factors made the situation quite prosperous, boosting the market atmosphere. As for the interest rates, they remained flat, but due to other needs for capital, there was a significant possibility of progress in the money market.

Interest Rate Prices: (Foreign Interest) The opening market interest rate was 7 mace, 2 fen, 5 li, 1 hao, 2 si, and a half. The afternoon market was 7 mace, 2 fen, 5 li, and 2 hao and a half, only about 2 hao and a half better than the previous day's market price. (Silver Interest) The opening market was 1 fen, 1 li, and the afternoon market was 1 fen, 4 li. Due to tighter collateral for head money transactions, there was an appearance of 1 fen, 2 li, and 3 si. Bank quotes also had 4 fen in the market.

Subsidiary Coin Market: There were no transactions in the Jiangnan small silver dollar market, so the price was the same as the previous afternoon, remaining at a blank bid of 6 mace, 4 fen, and 9 li and a half. The opening market for Guangdong small silver dollars was 6 mace, 4 fen, and 5 li and a half, and the afternoon market was 6 mace, 4 fen, 4 li, and 7 hao and a half, slightly down by half a li and 7 hao and a half compared to the previous day. The volume of transactions was 145,000 jiao in the morning and 60,000 jiao in the afternoon. Copper coins weakened by 1,500 wen, to 377,500 wen, with over 27,000 strings transacted.

Silver and Foreign Currency Inflow and Outflow: (Silver) Yesterday, the banks were quite busy with settlements. Chinese merchants settled over 4.1 million taels, foreign merchants settled 3.3 to 3.4 million taels, special settlements amounted to 3 to 4 million taels, and collateral transactions exceeded 1 million taels. Various goods, exchange taxes, and miscellaneous items settled over 11 million taels, with 1.2 million taels going into storage and 600,000 taels leaving. Japanese banks settled over 7.3 million taels in various items, with special settlements exceeding 1 million taels and 800,000 taels going into storage. Due to the settlement period, the money shops' and silver firms' single settlements were particularly large, totaling over 65.5 million taels. Silver head money settlements amounted to over 4.7 million taels, remittances from various routes were over 1.4 million taels, and cash disbursements were over 1 million taels. (Foreign Currency) Remittance drafts made 1.715 million in the morning and 1.645 million in the afternoon. Banknotes made 72,000 in the morning and 45,000 in the afternoon. Off-exchange banknotes made 185,000 in the morning and 130,000 in the afternoon. Foreign exchange between banks made 650,000 in the morning and 450,000 in the afternoon. Bank foreign currency account settlements were over 1.8 million, with banknote withdrawals and issuances of 3.3 to 3.4 million. Money shops' foreign currency settlements exceeded 13 million, foreign currency head money settlements were over 2.2 million, foreign currency lending and borrowing were over 1.8 million, small money shops' transactions exceeded 800,000, and inter-bank transactions were over 300,000.

Importers' Payment of Sterling Bills 192

According to financial circles, the money market may continue to rise. Yesterday, a large batch of sterling settlements was due, and the settlement of other large bills and various exchange transactions required a large amount of capital. Furthermore, the amount of foreign rice settlement was also significant. Even if there is not much speculation in the market, the circulation of head money will inevitably be tight. Although bank collateral has an appearance of being flexible, if the money market tightens, it may not be as desired. Therefore, it is predicted that the future money market, even if it does not rise sharply, will certainly not be as flat and loose as it used to be.

Yarn and Cotton: An Extraordinary Price Drop Occurs in the Yarn Market 194

This is a Reaction to the Drastic Changes in the World Cotton Industry

The yarn market has collapsed. A large increase in U.S. cotton production has caused the price of third-grade yarn to plummet by 13 yuan. Local market prices are higher than those in the past, and long positions are limited by quantity but not by price. As a result, selling orders are being shouted out loud. However, many small investors are entering the market because the price drop is too severe. Future demand is not expected to be very high because the floods in various regions are too severe, and farmers have less purchasing power. Therefore, those who are watching the global situation are still selling. However, some large merchants are making near-term sales and far-term purchases due to the rising gold prices, and they are taking a neutral position. It is feared that the 50 tael mark for local yarn will be difficult to maintain.

People's Standard Yarn Falls by More Than 5 Taels: At the opening of the People's Standard yarn market, the news of the deteriorating external cotton market caused many sellers to rush to sell, and Japanese merchants also sold. The price drop in each month was particularly severe, with each falling by 5 taels, 5 qian to 6 taels. In the afternoon, the market atmosphere calmed slightly due to the slight increase in gold prices, and prices rebounded by 3, 4, or 5 qian. The total volume of transactions was 94,000 bales. It was found that Changfeng sold 4,400 bales, Hengde sold 3,550 bales, Gengfeng sold 3,100 bales, Minghua sold 1,150 bales, Taixing sold 1,650 bales, Shenglong sold 2,850 bales, Dafeng sold 1,400 bales, and Meiji sold 1,850 bales. Xincheng bought 5,750 bales, Yiyu bought 3,650 bales, Fuhe bought 4,000 bales, Ruidai bought 4,700 bales, Yudai bought 3,900 bales, and Dafu bought 1,750 bales. The closing prices of People's Standard yarn are recorded on the left.

The Cotton Market Plummets 195

The Situation is Perilous... Selling is Unusually Strong

According to official reports, U.S. cotton production is 15,584,000 bales. The December contract on the Chicago Mercantile Exchange is at 6.8 cents, a sharp drop of 137 points. It is expected that the New York market price will collapse tomorrow, which is inevitable. Therefore, the market is extremely fearful. On the same day, Japanese merchants and Dongmian foreign firms sold a huge amount of 50,000 to 60,000 dan at market prices, and the market plummeted. However, some local merchants believe that the floods in various regions are severe, the weather is unfavorable, and there may be unrest. Also, gold prices are soaring, so they are still unwilling to close out their positions. Indian and American cotton foreign firms are selling at discounted prices at various factories, which are 6 to 7 taels lower than the previous day. However, the factories are aware that the world trend is unstable, so they have no intention of purchasing.

Han Standard Cotton Drops by 1 Tael, 6 or 7 Qian: At the opening of the Han Standard cotton market, the news of the unfavorable external cotton market and the sharp drop in the price of Japanese third-grade yarn by 4 Japanese yuan caused Japanese merchants in the market to sell in large quantities. Panic reached its peak, and prices in each month fell by 1 tael, 6, 7, or 8 qian to 2 taels. In the afternoon, prices rose by 1 or 2 qian, 5 fen in each month as gold prices strengthened. The total volume of transactions was 294,700 dan. It was found that Tianlong sold 12,000 dan, Gongtai sold 13,200 dan, Gengfeng sold 28,200 dan, Shenji sold 12,100 dan, Changfeng sold 8,200 dan, and Hengda sold 4,200 dan. Ruidai bought 13,600 dan, Xinheng bought 8,400 dan, Xincheng bought 10,200 dan, Yiyu bought 7,100 dan, Yuande bought 4,300 dan, Xiesheng bought 4,100 dan, Xinfeng bought 4,800 dan, and Dafu bought 3,900 dan. The closing prices are recorded on the left.

Spot Cotton Sales are Blocked: Spot cotton transactions are flat. It is estimated that the source is 1,280 bales of Yaohua cotton.

Rice brand "Te Ling" 37.5 and brand "Di Zhen Xin" factory entered 200 lots of spot goods to the warehouse.

Second U.S. Cotton Government Report 197

Washington, 8th: The second U.S. cotton crop report was officially released at noon today by the Department of Agriculture's Cotton Reporting Office. The production situation is 74.9% of the normal annual production, totaling 15,584,000 bales. The reports from the same period in the previous five years are also listed below (in thousands):

Grains: New Japonica Rice Rises Another Half 199

True High-Quality White Japonica Rice Opens at 19 Yuan in Secret Market

Wangdian New Early Indica Rice Opens at 14 Yuan, 4 Jiao

South Market: The origin of various groups is approximately 5 to 6 days away, and there are few river stocks. Sales in urban and rural stores are seeing a shortage of goods. However, sellers are holding onto their goods and selling them because yesterday's prices were not satisfactory, and the market is tense. Transactions have increased. Later, after the Social Affairs Bureau issued an order to implement price limits, people felt slightly calmer. Therefore, the prices of various goods are still being evaluated automatically, and they are 5 jiao higher than yesterday. The situation is bound to improve further as goods remain scarce and sales are active. However, the situation may be slightly worse after the evaluation. Yesterday, 40 shi of Dongxin japonica rice arrived, and sales were still good, with the price opening at 16 yuan and a half. Over 100 shi of Wangdian new early rice arrived from the previous day, and the price opened at 14 yuan and 4 jiao. Foreign rice goods are still scarce, and Hanban continues to move, making the market even stronger.

New Gate: Very few goods arrive from the interior. Transactions on this street are not very prosperous. Furthermore, it is heard that there are floods in various places, making people even more nervous. Because the Social Affairs Bureau issued an order to limit prices, the highest price of white japonica rice cannot exceed 17 yuan. Recently, there has been a lack of accumulation in the river, which is actually due to the customer's investment. Special goods with three [unclear characters] are offered at 19 yuan, and the shopkeepers pay 2 yuan per shi. Northern japonica rice, thin rice, foreign pointy rice, reed pointy rice, and pier pointy rice have each risen by 7 or 8 jiao. Yesterday, 2 bundles of glutinous rice arrived and were sold out immediately, with the market tending to tighten by 2 jiao. The new japonica rice is similar to that in the southern market.

Flour Price Rises Sharply by 4 and a Half Fen 200

Yesterday, the flour market suddenly saw a huge surge. The reason for the excitement is that since the floods in various places, grain prices have gradually skyrocketed. Recently, flour and wheat have been relatively inexpensive. Therefore, after the opening price, the Yangtze River, the inland, and various groups are rushing to buy without price limits. This month's highest price has soared to 2 taels, 1 qian, 6 fen and a half, September to 2 taels and 2 qian, October to 2 taels, 2 qian and 3 fen, November to 2 taels, 2 qian, 4 fen and a half, December to 2 taels and 2 qian and a half, and January to 2 taels, 2 qian and 4 fen, which are all 5 to 6 fen higher than the previous day's closing price. However, the Tianjin group and factories are selling back in large quantities, so the price has fallen back by 2 or 3 fen in the middle, but it has rebounded again due to the strong demand. The total volume of transactions in the city has reached 2.5 to 2.6 million, which seems to be a new record. In the future, it is necessary to see the extent of the floods in order to predict the intentions of the inland groups. As a result, this month's price is 2 fen, 7 li and a half higher than the previous week, September's price is 3 fen, 7 li and a half higher, October's price is 4 fen and a half higher, and November to January are each 4 fen and 2 li and a half higher.

Wheat Market Sees Strong Buying Interest 201

Near-Term Prices Surge by 1 Qian, 2 Fen

Yesterday's wheat market saw a continuous surge. Although foreign wheat prices had small fluctuations of 2, 3, 4, or 5 jiao, the inland Yangtze River group believed that the floods were extremely severe. Although there were large quantities of foreign wheat scheduled, it was feared that they would not be enough to compensate for the losses caused by the floods. Furthermore, the exchange rate was also shrinking, and the future was bleak. There was a strong momentum to continue the surge. Therefore, buying interest was strong and unstoppable. Given this situation, it would not be surprising if prices rise further. As a result, this month's price is 1 qian, 2 fen higher than the previous week, September's price is 1 qian, 1 fen higher, October's price is 9 fen higher, and November and December's prices are 7 fen higher. Because spot wheat is scarce, the highest quality has been priced at 4 taels, 8 qian and 2 fen, an average increase of about 4 or 5 fen. It is estimated that 2,400 bales of Zhenjiang, Yizheng, Taicang, Penglai, Wusong, Zhichang, Kunshan, Anqing, Pudong, and Chongming wheat were handled by Huafeng and Fuxin.

Sugar Market: Various Sugars Rise with the Exchange Rate 202

Nearly 10,000 Bags of Spot Coarse Granulated White Sugar Open

Yesterday, there were still no reports from sugar-producing areas. In the public market, prices rose because of the sudden increase in the exchange rate, and the market atmosphere strengthened. Transactions were active, and prices rose gradually. Dutch sugar 24-grade coarse granulated white sugar was priced from 11 taels, 3 qian and a half to 4 qian and a half. Slightly higher prices were 11 taels, 5 qian and a half to 6 qian. 20-grade medium granulated white sugar was 11 taels and 05 fen, and 10-grade Dutch red sugar was 9 taels and 7 qian. The market was also brisk. Transactions of Taikoo sugar were quite active. B grade was priced from 12 taels and 1 qian to 1 qian and a half, CW grade was 11 taels and 9 qian to 9 qian and a half, new goods were 12 taels, HX grade was 11 taels and 7 qian and a half, and HM grade was 11 taels and 4 qian to 4 qian. Deliveries were scarce, and the trend was still brisk. The market saw Huaxin offering 3,000 bags of spot coarse granulated white sugar at 11 taels and 4 qian and a half, and 700 bags of 10-grade Dutch red sugar at 9 taels and 7 qian and a half. Zhenxiang sold over 5,000 bags of coarse granulated white sugar at 11 taels and 5 qian. Maochang sold 699 bags of bowl green sugar at 8 taels and 7 qian. The industry was eager to buy, and all were sold, making the market extremely brisk.

North and South Goods: Black Melon Seeds Rise Due to Floods 203

Recently, black melon seeds have seen price increases because there have been floods in the producing areas, and the harvest is bound to be poor. The market trend is strong. Current market prices for first-grade goods such as Jizhong seeds are 17 taels, middle-grade goods such as Xukui seeds are 14 taels and a half, and lower-grade goods such as Dalian seeds are 11 taels to 10 taels. In recent days, groups from Changsha, Fuzhou, and Shantou have been purchasing a lot of lower-grade goods. Because the new goods are scarce, various firms are unwilling to sell much of their inventory, so prices may rise again in the future.

Book and Newspaper Introduction

An Introduction to Social Sciences 226

— Hong

By Mei Yonggeng

Written by Guo Renyuan

The rise of social sciences is only a matter of the last few decades. Nowadays, in Chinese writing circles, treatises on social sciences are emerging like a storm. Many of them are specialized studies of this emerging science.

The book I am going to introduce to readers now is Guo's "An Introduction to Social Sciences".

Social science is a collection of various sciences that study the various phenomena of social life and seek their theorems and laws. The organization of human groups themselves, political activities, and economic activities all have very complex ties. In China today, when the tide of the Great Revolution is surging and destroying the inherent social organization, a kind of unrest is appearing in society. Of course, we should find methods of self-rescue in the social sciences.

In the human social life of the twentieth century, connections with each other are becoming increasingly close. The rise and fall of gold prices in the United States can affect the life of a small peasant family in inland China. In short, since the economic organization has formed a global system, from national political wars to people's daily lives of food and drink, men and women, there are close relationships. The phenomenon where moving one hair affects the whole body is the real phenomenon of today's society. We should find solutions to all these problems in the social sciences.

We also know that revolution is two-sided. One side is political and economic, while the other is the removal of the inherent and decadent thoughts in the minds of the masses. The former can generally be said to have been completed after the National Revolutionary Army unified the country, while the latter is the work of the period of political tutelage, which is being implemented but has not yet achieved considerable results. The only way to remedy this is to make efforts to instill knowledge of contemporary social science to the general public so they can understand the current political, economic, and social conditions and strive for new creations.

The greatest advantage of Guo's Introduction to Social Sciences lies in his use of a mixed method to edit, so that beginners know that social phenomena are interrelated. The author says in the preface:

"...Social life is originally a whole and complete entity, but this phenomenon is extremely complex. People divide society into several kinds for the convenience of research. However, this kind of classification is most unsuitable for beginners, because it is feared that beginners cannot understand the integrity and wholeness of social phenomena. This book, in order to avoid this danger, uses a mixed method to edit..."

That's right, the learning of social science is like the boundless and shoreless sea. Beginners often only see fragments and independent parts of social phenomena, and do not know that political, economic, legal, and other phenomena are interrelated and interact with each other, and are not independent of each other. This book can give readers a holistic concept of social phenomena.

Secondly, the advantage of this book lies only in talking about the facts of social life, and avoiding academic discussions as much as possible. The author focuses on narrating social life, rarely participating in any opinions, or making any claims. I feel that scholars who write social science books will inevitably make beginners feel lost in a fog if they focus on academic theories. Therefore, beginners should read books that focus on facts. This book is a book that focuses on the facts of social life and avoids academic discussions as much as possible. This is another advantage of this book.

This book is an introductory book to social science, so its content only makes a concise description, which is most suitable for general beginners.

New Book Information 227

World Economy and Industrial Rationalization: The current world economic panic is a major issue that agitates the whole world. Therefore, all countries are trying to save it. Mr. Zeng Guangxun, the editor of Social Magazine, has seen this, and has written the book World Economy and Industrial Rationalization based on his research, so as to provide a common study. The book is divided into two parts. The upper part describes the general situation of the world economy, from the development of productivity to the occurrence of the world economic panic, and then to the demise of capitalism. The lower part describes the essence of industrial rationalization, and clearly explains the actual situation of the rationalization movement in various countries. The book has a very detailed description of the world economy and the Chinese economy in 1930. It also describes in detail the important issues in the world economic community in the first half of 1931, such as the German-Austrian customs union and the Hoover debt extension plan. Looking at the whole book, the materials are rich and novel, and the judgment is clear and correct. It is a book that those who study the world economy and care about China's economic construction issues must read. The book has been printed and will be published soon. To request a sample copy, you can write to Social Magazine at No. 155, Yonganli, North Sichuan Road, Shanghai, and it will be sent to you.

The Liming Bookstore on Wangping Street, Four Horse Road, recently published a book on the Principles and Practices of Accounting, written by American accounting expert Frank H. Strieghthoff, and jointly translated by Li Mingshou and Zhang Zhongliang. The original book is used as a textbook in various specialized schools and above in the United States. Two Chinese accounting experts, Pan Xulun and economic expert Li Quanshi, have highly praised it in their prefaces, so its value can be known. For all major middle schools that use textbooks for the accounting subject, this book is most suitable. The bureau also published a book on vocational education, written by Xiong Zirong. This book elaborates on the theory and methods of vocational education, as well as the problems of vocational guidance in primary and secondary schools. It can be used as a textbook for general vocational schools, and a good reference book for those who study vocational education.

Social News

An Eighty-Five-Year-Old Female Reporter 228

— Hong

Mrs. Alice Van Sickle of Ohio, USA, is the oldest and most active female reporter in the United States. She is already eighty-five years old this year, but she is still very enthusiastic about this profession. Many of her words and deeds are very interesting and worthy of our attention.

She is now a reporter for five newspapers in Ohio. She also reports news on the radio every week. The ears of thousands of housewives can often hear her voice. She also writes articles for the prisoners' newspaper and often goes to talk to prisoners.

She lives in a simple little house in Covington. She is busy all day long, so her back is bent, she walks with a cane, and her hair has turned white, but her eyes are still bright.

She is indeed a talented journalist. She wrote a love story at the age of fourteen and published it in a weekly, and from then on she began her lifelong career.

After she got married, many other things took away her time and energy, and life was uneasy, almost interrupting her lifelong career, but because of her firm will, it never stopped.

She has often helped others throughout her life, helping her father, helping her sick husband to support the family, and taking care of housework. Once, the owner of a newspaper was attacked because he owed wages, and she helped him work day and night. She was the first woman to join the American Printing Industry Union.

She has published a lot about her philosophy of age.

She said, "Whether men or women, after middle age, they are always unwilling to continue to pursue the success they did not get in their early years. This is not because of the loss of their physical or mental strength, but because their desires are less than before, and their goals are gradually weakened. In fact, the rewards obtained from the loss of physical and mental strength, 丨丨rich experience, correct judgment, and mature intelligence, 丨丨are sometimes more than lost."

"The difficulty is that after the age of forty-five or fifty, many people are unwilling to try again. They have no intention of doing things that they are still capable of doing, so they stop working, they admit weakness, and they get old. The reason why I can maintain my youth is entirely because I continue to work. This is undoubtedly."

In the 1929 Ohio Women Journalists Association, her article won first prize. She said, "If you are willing to work for a long time, you will definitely be successful. The reason why I was able to get the first prize this time is because I have spent sixty years of effort on this path."

She has devoted herself to a writing career for 70 years, but she still has no intention of retiring. She said, "If you think you are satisfied with the career you have achieved, then of course you can retire. If you are not satisfied with what you have achieved, then why do you want to retire? It is best to continue to work hard."

She also said, "Old age is not only happier than younger age, but also more interesting and more successful. Age is an asset. It makes me understand life."

China's Silk Exports Decrease Significantly 229

Due to Poor Spring Cocoon Harvest

According to investigations, this year's exports of Chinese raw silk have decreased by 62% for Shanghai silk and 52% for Guangdong silk compared with the same period last year. That is, from June 1st to July 19th, Shanghai silk, including machine silk and Qili silk, totaled 8,012 packages, while the same period last year was 20,428 packages. The reason is due to the poor spring cocoon harvest. Factors such as fluctuations in the silver market and the decline in the price of Japanese silk had little impact. Also, Guangdong silk (from May 1st to July 15th) this year was 8,599 packages, compared to 18,787 packages last year. The reasons for the decrease are that the quality is not good and consumers are not very welcome, and the price of Japanese silk is low.

Research on Ash-Made Fuel 230

Adopted by the Japanese Railway Bureau

According to a Japanese report, the fuel used for fire maintenance in each locomotive in the Japanese National Railway Bureau's engine depot has long been a problem. Now the Nagoya engine depot has made fuel for fire maintenance from Kinta (incompletely burned powder of coal) which used to be a problem on the disposal site. That is, briquettes made by mixing 70% Kinta, 20% powder of the first kind of briquettes used by various specialized locomotives, and 10% clay, have been adopted since the beginning of June. The engine depot has many locomotives assigned to it, and the average daily savings is about 900 yuan by using waste instead of coal. The Nagoya Railway Bureau plans to purchase a briquette manufacturing machine immediately and start large-scale manufacturing. The entire bureau uses about 100,000 yuan per year. If all the bureaus across the country adopt it, it can save more than 500,000 yuan.

US Unemployment to Reach 7 Million 231

Conditions this Winter May Be Worse than Last Winter - President Hoover is Discussing Relief Methods

Washington News: The American Federation of Labor announced that the number of unemployed workers increased again in July. It is expected that the number of unemployed people in the United States will reach 7 million this winter. Also, the employment index in July was 18.9, June was 18.2, and May was 17.1. Federation President Green said, "If the number of unemployed people increases as usual, there will be 7 million people without work this winter, and the unemployment situation this winter will definitely be worse than last winter. The National Community Treasury Association's survey of unemployment in 184 cities predicts that relief expenses will have to be doubled from last winter." Green urged immediate engagement in relief.

Another report: Washington officials expect that the trend of salary reductions in the American industry this winter will become a widespread phenomenon. Relief methods are still being discussed. President Hoover specially summoned Red Cross President Payne to the White House to discuss methods of cooperation between various charitable organizations. According to Payne's observation, the unemployment situation is not very bad, and this winter may not be worse than last winter.

France's Foreign Trade Deficit Increases Sharply 232

The Deficit Reaches Over 5 Trillion Francs - The Industry is Greatly Disturbed

Paris News: According to the Director-General of Taxation, France's foreign trade deficit continues to increase sharply. In the first five months of this year, imports totaled 19,287,549,000 francs, and exports totaled 1373,910,000 francs. The deficit reached 5,565,639,000 francs. The French industry is greatly worried about this. In February and March of this year, French exports were still considered stable, but they suddenly fell in May. The import price for that month was 3,574,706,000 francs, and the export price was 2,438,165,000 francs. The deficit reached 1,136,541,000 francs. Also, in the first five months of this year, compared with the same period last year, imports decreased by 3,383,000 francs and exports decreased by 5,528,000 francs.

Number of Cars in Various Countries 233

Ranked in Order: US, UK, France, Germany, Canada

According to a survey by the British Automobile Manufacturers and Sales Association, the United States still ranks first in the number of cars in the world, followed by the United Kingdom, France, Germany, and Canada. The survey by the association is based on the figures for the past year (1930), including pedal cars. The list is as follows:

United States: 26,746,184 vehicles

United Kingdom: 1,484,92 vehicles

France: 1,322,387 vehicles

Germany: 688,633 vehicles

Canada: 1,179,817 vehicles

Foch's Diary of the European War by a French General 234

— Translated by Gu Angruo

I intend to submit the following plan (July 24, 1918):

(1)

The German army's fifth offensive since the start of the war was thwarted, resulting in complete failure.

The French Tenth and Sixth Armies took the offensive and defeated the German army.

Our army must take advantage of this victory and pursue relentlessly with all its strength. The impact of this will far exceed the significance of this particular battle.

(2)

The enemy's defeat has become the basis for the Allied forces to plan their operational strategies.

The current situation of the enemy and our forces is as follows:

Our army has already achieved an equal number of troops to the enemy, but our army still does not have an advantage in the total number of divisions.

The German army, compelled by the situation, has had to mobilize so many divisions to fight. For the first time, our reserve forces have the upper hand. Furthermore, since the enemy has been forced to withdraw many exhausted divisions from the front lines for rest and recuperation, our army will also have the same advantage in the number of fresh reserve troops.

Moreover, all intelligence indicates that the enemy has divided its troops into two parts: one part with weak strength, used to hold the defensive line and dedicated to sacrifice; the other part stationed behind this weak defensive line, deploying response measures. Although this army has been carefully trained by the German High Command, its combat effectiveness has been greatly affected.

The Allied air force and tank artillery are also overwhelmingly superior. After the arrival of the American artillery corps, our army's strength in artillery will certainly be greatly increased.

Finally, in the rear of the Allied forces, 250,000 American troops arrive in France every month like a tide, becoming a powerful reserve force. On the enemy's side, we already know that he once adopted emergency measures to relieve the panic of troop replenishment in May. Now he is encountering even greater difficulties in maintaining the strength of the armies on the front lines, and signs of a new panic are emerging.

In terms of materials, our army is gradually gaining the upper hand. Since the start of the war, although the enemy has launched fierce attacks with unprecedented force, they have ultimately failed to achieve the decisive victory they needed to achieve. Our army has always been able to maintain morale, and now after the great victory, morale is even more invigorated.

The overall situation of the Great War has reached a turning point. The Allied forces have progressed to a position of turning danger into safety and changing from defense to offense. The Allied troop strength and operational doctrine allow it to maintain this offensive advantage.

The Allied forces have always been forced to adopt a defensive posture due to a lack of troops, and now the time has come to switch to an offensive stance. (To be continued)
